==PAGE:165==
Chapter 8
Discussion
Throughout this thesis, several aspects have been aﬀected. The results for which
will now be discussed. The main aspect, during the preparation of creating a
superstructure, is the residual capacity analysis. It can be discussed whether
just three buildings are enough to establish a realistic picture of the building
styles, habits, and potential for the period. However, the three houses of choice
are located under three diﬀerent building methods, concerning the period. They
present three diﬀerent types of bearing material, as well as three diﬀerent static
systems. So even-though, this thesis narrows its focus on three properties, they
together create a nice framework of the period of construction due to their
diversity.
House 1, which represents traditional constructions, starts out with overloaded
existing conditions, and thus no useful residual capacity is left for the superstruc-
ture. However, the fact that the result yields overload of the main partition wall
and the outer walls, does not give rise to concern. Since, the assumption that
the existing roof is disregarded when removed, during a potential renovation,
makes the result of the facades appear more critical. In addition, the property
has existed for more than 60 years, without any negligence of any form, which
may indicate that today’s calculations underestimate the strengths of existing
masonry.
Masonry/ traditional construction techniques have been used for many years.
==PAGE:166==
154
Discussion
Therefore, it has been possible to optimize the construction potential, whilst
minimizing the amount of bearing force. Thus, there is no residual capacity to
exploit, when establishing a new superstructure. As concrete construction has
just initiated its way into the market, it is a new and therefore not optimized
technique, providing that the properties have large volumes of residual capacity.
Since it is clear, that it would be irresponsible to build to the capacity limit,
when using a new construction method like concrete.
One other reason for the high residual capacity in concrete structures, is due
to the fact that the smallest dimension is determined by rewarding ﬁre require-
ments at the time of construction, and not after critical load capacity. Which
is substantiated by the results of the ﬁre investigation. This is seen, because
the diﬀerence between ﬁre protection, of the period of 1950-1980 compared with
today, is not conspicuous. Hence, there is no major changes to be made in the
existing conditions, to upgrade them to fulﬁll modern requirements. For this
reason, the majority of the ﬁre analysis, in this thesis, concerns the superstruc-
ture and overall ﬁre conditions of the properties.
By a closer inspection of masonry vs.
concrete, the results are not up to a
major discussion. Concrete constructions from the period 1950-1980 are more
open regarding a superstructure than masonry buildings.
The result of the
traditional masonry construction, House 1, is so critical, that it can be discussed
whether it is ever economically feasible to establish a superstructure. This is
due to the fact that, in order for a superstructure to be realized, the bearing
system must be highly reinforced; or the superstructure must be worn by a new
bearing system. No matter what solution is followed, this will greatly aﬀect the
existing construction and its residents. That is, in addition to the cost of the
actual renovation, a signiﬁcant cost for rehousing or reimbursing of the existing
residents is unavoidable. It is estimated that the total cost vs. the gain will not
be beneﬁcial. Which also forms the basis for the absence of a concrete solution
for House 1 in this research.
The main diﬀerence between the two concrete buildings is, the slabs of House 2
are a double-sided plate, which means that all sides are bearing. This is not the
case for House 3. In the third house only the transverse inner walls function as
bearing parts. In addition, there columns are established in the facades of House
2. However, despite the diﬀerence in the static system, the results of the two
properties are almost identical. If the construction consists of concrete elements
or cast on site, it has a high residual capacity. This creates a good foundation for
a superstructure, which can thus be done without any intervention in existing
conditions. With the choice of modular construction, as building concept for
the superstructure, the need for refurbishment is also reduced/ eliminated. This
is due to the short construction process on the site, and that the construction is
carried out without scaﬀold to the detriment of existing residents. Additionally,
==PAGE:167==
155
the most important parts of the building are manufactured at the factory, so
the noise levels are also minimal when building with modules.
It is therefore important to discuss and consider the various options for choice of
superstructure. Of course, it can always be discussed whether modular construc-
tion is the most optimal solution for the superstructure. As the modules consist
of wooden elements.
This creates a conﬂict in relation to ﬁre optimization,
where other types of materials would be signiﬁcantly better. On the other hand
modular construction, as mentioned above, is particularly advantageous when
taking into account the existing residents. The existing buildings also creates a
limit to exploit the full potential of modular constructions, as the modules must
be adapted to the existing conditions, in which staircase investment in existing
properties is important. With existing staircases in the middle of the property,
as was the case of House 2, it is very diﬃcult to get the modules to ﬁt around.
Which is also one of the reasons why not all of the stairs are continued in the
solution to this case.
The design of the chosen solution proposal is also up for discussion.
These
solutions could be designed at many diﬀerent ways and it is not necessarily, the
most optimal solution implemented in this project. This is because of the focus
on making three diﬀerent solutions with diﬀerent forecasting points. This focus
was chosen to show the wide range of options available when refurbishing, despite
the fact that the solution must be established within the framework of existing
structures. In addition, the construction of lifts to the existing properties are
also established diﬀerently for the three properties.
Depending on what the
desire for the elevator is, it can be established in diﬀerent ways, below the
various conditions for the possibilities, illustrated in this thesis, are collected;
House 1: The elevators are established outside of the existing building, two elevators
for the entire property. Therefore, no square meters of the property is
included. In this solution, the elevator is available for all residents, both
existing and new. In addition, it is not associated with stairs and can
therefore be dimensioned to evacuate in case of ﬁre, if desired and used as
rescue lifts for the rescue crew.
House 2: There is an elevator in every third entrance, inside the property. Thus,
quadratic meters are revoked in a few of the existing apartments. Likewise,
this does not mean that all existing residents are in favor of the elevator,
but all new apartments have access to the lifts. The lifts are established in
a separate ﬁre department, and can therefore also be used for evacuation
and rescue in case of ﬁre.
House 3: In each entrance an elevator is connected to the existing staircase. Thus,
quadratic meters are included in all existing apartments, on the other
==PAGE:168==
156
Discussion
hand, all existing as well as new residents gets the pleasure of the elevator.
As the elevator is established in continuation of the staircase, they are
connected to each-others ﬁre sections and the lifts will therefore not be
able, to be used for ﬁre either as evacuation or rescue.
In order to make the most out of the module building potential, it has a great
inﬂuence how many diﬀerent modules are used and how much redundancy they
provide. As illustrated in Figure 4.3, it is seen that you want to get at least 10
identical modules, in order to achieve highest proﬁt. In Table 8.1, the number
of modules, for the selected solution for House 2 and 3 are shown. The ﬁrst row
shows the number of modules required for a single solution, in the second row
the number of modules required for an solution covering the entire cadastral is
shown. The table shows that, as described in the report, the one-plan solution
used in House 2 is somewhat more optimal than the shifted plan solution used
in House 3, if only the number of modules in the existing properties are viewed.
However, it should be said that House 2 is nine entrances long, whereas House 3
is only four entrances long. The reason behind why the second row is shown, ie.
the entire cadastral, is to show how large the potential for superstructures are in
these types of properties. It is not a coincidence that these properties coexists
with other buildings on the same cadastral. In fact, it is actually characteristic
for buildings from this period. For House 2 there are two blocks of three ﬂoors
more on the cadastral and around House 3 there are six blocks with four ﬂoors.
The solution proposals could be transferred to these properties with only small
change due to diﬀerent number of entrances.
Table 8.1: Number of modules used for the diﬀerent solutions for House 2 &
House 3. The numbers are shown for only the investigated building
and the sum for all relevant buildings within the cadastral.

==PAGE:169==
Chapter 9
Conclusion
In order to classify the apartment buildings constructed in Denmark during the
period of 1950-1980, basic knowledge about this period have been presented.
This knowledge have been supported by three concrete properties.
Each of
which represents diﬀerent construction techniques used in the period. That is
masonry, insitu, and concrete elements. To illuminate the underlying techniques,
the three buildings have been subject to thorough investigation, in the form of:
• On site visual inspection of the construction
• Collection- and analysis of the available archive material
• In depth residual capacity investigations
• Concise ﬁre analysis of the existing construction
This exploration grounded the engineering framework for extending the existing
buildings with modern superstructures. It was readily concluded, that concrete
based constructions provided great potential for superstructures, whereas the
traditional masonry constructions did not. Masonry apartment constructions
are simply so optimized, that there is no residual capacity left.
==PAGE:170==
158
Conclusion
This paper brieﬂy touched upon some of the measurements available for reinforc-
ing the existing construction, in order to provide the bearing capacity needed by
the masonry constructions in order to support superstructures. However, this
would require a major renovation of the existing building, making the creation
of superstructures unfeasible. Contrary, the concrete constructions, from the
period, sustain a surprisingly high residual capacity. Thus, this type of build-
ings provides optimal conditions for designing and creation of superstructures.
This thesis documented the creation of three leveled superstructures. The super-
structures was created using lightweight materials, allowing the entire extension
to be created without interference or reinforcement of the existing load bear-
ing system. What is more, the superstructures was created with three diﬀerent
design goals, underlining the ﬂexibility:
• To enhance the existing construction potential as much as possible.
• To minimize the nuisance towards the existing residents.
• To optimize and create attractive balconies.
Based on the ﬁre analysis and legislation, it can be concluded that the ﬁre safety,
during 1950-1980 compared with today, have not undertaken major changes for
this types of buildings.
This was reﬂected by ﬁreprooﬁng of the properties,
which were not critical. All properties meet the criteria from the time of con-
struction and can easily be upgraded to present requirements, regarding six
storey apartment buildings, without major intervention. The biggest challenge
in relation to ﬁre safety was thus to get the wooden modules in the superstruc-
ture to meet the requirements.
The ﬁre protection varies from structure to
structure, however the most comprehensive assessment consists of four layers of
ﬁre gypsum. However, the ﬁre analyses does not only concern post ﬂash-over
ﬁre safety. A pre ﬂash-over ﬁre safety analysis have been conducted as well.
In addition, three diﬀerent ﬁre scenarios have been studied, to check if the ﬁre
safety based on prescriptive based ﬁre safety is suﬃcient. The results shows that
the overall evacuation of the buildings is not critical, however the evacuation
from the aﬀected ﬁre cell is. If the residents in the aﬀected ﬁre cell does not
react upon ﬁre immediately, they will not get to a safe place within the building
before critical conditions occurs. However this is a normal result for apartment
buildings, because of the relatively high amount of ﬂammable material leading
the ﬁre to spread fast.
Nowadays regulations requires the presence of elevators in apartment construc-
tions above three ﬂoors. Therefore, the problem of establishing elevators in the
existing properties has been investigated. Elevators can be designed in a variety
of ways depending on the features desired by the lifts. Likewise, the solution
==PAGE:171==
159
depends signiﬁcantly on the design of the superstructure, as well as the layout of
the existing construction. Since it is not useful to establish lifts in eg. a kitchen
or bath, as this will result in a challenge relocating these rooms.
As mentioned, this thesis chose to construct the superstructures using lightweight
wooden modules. However, it is important to understand that these modules is
not a stock product, and they do not determine the ﬂoor plan. In fact, when
extending an existing construction horizontally most of the ﬂoor layout is prede-
termined. Hence, a major task is given of maximizing the module redundancy,
whilst satisfying the existing conditions. This task would be smaller when con-
structing a new building. Since the engineers are able to adjust all parameters
as needed. This is however not possible in the domain of refurbishing.
As said, the existing construction of the building locks some parameters regard-
ing the design of a potential superstructure. Thereby it is not said, that it is
not possible to mix architectonic design and renovation. In all three cases, sim-
ple 3D models have been prepared for the selected solution. Ascertaining that
the possibilities for designing of superstructure are many, despite the fact that
the framework from the existing buildings must be respected. In addition, this
thesis presented multiple proposals for apartment layouts, illustrating that the
design of the building does not impose any restrictions towards its residents.
The apartment layout was designed for students, disabled people, and families.
Since, all the solution proposals dealt with three-leveled superstructures built
on three leveled buildings, this thesis managed to double the amount of square
meters. In other words, twice as many apartments could be created, if the same
divisions was used.
However, as it is desired that larger multileveled apart-
ments should provide comfort for families, the resulting apartment potential of
this solution provided 2/3 of the existing.
Generally, it can be concluded that similar masonry apartment constructions
from the relevant period provides no direct potential for sustaining superstruc-
tures. However, concrete-, element-, and insitu constructions have a great po-
tential for superstructures. This yields better options and possibilities towards
urban renewal using existing buildings. Additionally, constructions of this type
often coexists in clusters, which means that several buildings could be expanded
using the same solution, maximizing the beneﬁts of the modular building tech-
niques.
==PAGE:172==
160
Conclusion
9.1
Future work
This project provides the basis for creating superstructures on existing apart-
ment buildings built in Denmark during the period of 1950-1980, with main
focus on bearing capacity and ﬁre safety. However, these conditions are not the
only ones, that are relevant and interesting regarding this subject. Topics that
are not highlighted in this project and which could be intriguing to dive into
could be:
• To perform samples of existing bearing structures. That is, do they match
the calculation results or are the strength of the existing constructions
underestimated/ overestimated?
• To look into the existing foundation. Does it have suﬃcient bearing ca-
pacity for a superstructure. If not, how can these be enhanced optimally?
• To investigate the energy conditions of the existing buildings. How is it
possible to make an energy upgrade of the existing building in connection
with a superstructure?

Cembrit Solid fremstilles som rektangulære plader i 
to formater – 1192x2500 mm og 1192x3050 mm, 
pladetykkelsen er 8 mm.
Materiale
Cembrit Solid består af cement, mineralsk filler, 
PVA- og cellulosefibre.
Farveægthed
Fibercement er et naturmateriale, og nuanceforskelle 
kan forekomme som følge af de farveforskelle, der er 
i råvarerne. Dette har ingen indflydelse på holdbar­
heden af pladerne. For at minimere nuanceforskelle 
anbefales det, at plader, som skal monteres på den 
samme facade, tages fra samme produktion. 
Med tiden vil farver forandres som en konsekvens af 
påvirkninger fra UV lys og miljøet generelt. Cembrit 
Solid plader vil dog i høj grad bibeholde farve og glans.
I henhold til den Europæiske standard EN 20105 
- A02 vil farverne, efter 3.000 timers QUV test, 
bevare trin 4-5 efter farveægthedsskemaet. Dette 
betyder, at farven beholder sin nuance, og at en evt. 
forandring i farvedybden vil blive kategoriseret som 
knap synlig (jf. skemaet).
Skala til klassificering af ændring
Tilbehør
Til Cembrit Solid er der udviklet en komplet serie af 
tilbehør, som sikrer en simpel montage og et perfekt 
resultat med en meget lang holdbarhed. Pladerne 
kan leveres projektspecifikt på fixmål med alle 
skårne kanter forseglet. Ved tilskæring på bygge-
plads skal alle skårne kanter forsegles med Cembrit 
kantforsegler.
Farveægthed
Materialer
5
Ingen forandring
4
Ubetydelig forandring i farve-
dybde. Knap synlig
3
Tab af farvedybde. Synlig 
2
Øget forandring
1
Stor forandring
Cembrit Solid er en gennemfarvet fibercementplade med en fulddækkende overflade­
maling. Pladen er meget farveægte og leveres altid med skårne og forseglede kanter.

Gyproc GFE 15 PROTECT® F Ergo
Gyproc GF 15 PROTECT® F
Produktbeskrivelse
900 og 1200 mm bred Brandgipsplade med overflade af karton og 
glasfiberarmeret gipskerne. Pladen yder bedre brandmodstand end en 
almindelig gipsplade, da den bliver siddende på konstruktionen i læn­
gere tid. Pladen fungerer som fastholdelse af isolering (også granulat) 
i såvel vandrette som lodrette konstruktioner.
Anvendelsesområde
Gyproc GFE 15 Protect F Ergo og Gyproc GF 15 Protect F anvendes 
primært i konstruktioner med høje brandkrav som beklædning på 
bærende træskeletvægge i fleretageshuse, etagedæk, skaktvægge, in­
dervægge og som indvendig beklædning på bærende og ikke bærende 
stålskelet ydervægge.
Kantudførelse
Pladen har kartonbeklædt, forsænkede langkant og savet, ret kort­
kant. Langkantenes forsænkning er beregnet for samlingspartling til 
jævn overflade.
Montering
Gyproc GFE 15 Protect F Ergo og Gyproc GF 15 Protect F monteres
i 1 - 3 lag på underlag af stål eller træprofiler.
